The Company considers funds flow from operations a key measure as it 
demonstrates the Company&#146;s ability to generate the cash necessary to fund 
future
growth through capital investment and to repay debt. Funds flow should not be 
considered an alternative to, or more meaningful than, net earnings as 
determined
in accordance with Canadian GAAP.</TD>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>WEST KAYBOB</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Production volumes
for the third quarter in the West Kaybob Operating Unit were 3,021 Boe/d
comprised of 14 MMcf/d of natural gas and 616 Bbl/d of oil and natural gas 
liquids. This is a six
percent increase over second quarter 2005 production rates of 2,840 Boe/d 
comprised of 13 MMcf/d of
natural gas and 694 Bbl/d of oil and natural gas liquids. Third quarter volumes 
were expected to
be significantly higher, however our drilling successes were offset by a wet 
summer that restricted
road use and field access resulting in production and construction delays.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Third quarter 2005 
capital spending including land was $20.5&nbsp;million, bringing annual capital
spending to $66.6&nbsp;million for the West Kaybob Operating Unit. Paramount has
budgeted $95&nbsp;million
for the capital spending program in the West Kaybob area for 2005. The fourth 
quarter capital
spending program will be focused on executing our operated and non-operated 
drilling programs, with
an aggressive completion and construction effort during the winter months.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount 
participated in the drilling of 8 (3.1 net) wells in the area during the 
quarter; all
wells were cased for potential gas production. Two wells were operated by 
Paramount while the
remaining six wells were drilled by third parties. Paramount has participated in
the drilling of
32 (9.8 net) wells to date in West Kaybob and plans to participate in the 
drilling of up to 18 (9.0
net) additional wells for the remainder of the year; seven of which will be 
operated by the
Company. These wells are all multi-zone production candidates; up to six zones 
per well.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount added to 
its significant land holdings in the deep basin. In the third quarter $4.9
million was spent on Crown land acquisitions bringing the total for the year to 
$22.0&nbsp;million.
This land investment will provide Paramount with new drilling opportunities as 
well as additional
leverage for future land negotiations. With an aggressive strategy planned for 
the shut-in gas, we
are confident that we can make up the production shortfalls in the next six 
months. We estimate
there is approximately 1,000 Boe/d of shut-in production that may be tied-in 
when surface
conditions improve. There are also plans to install two field compressors in the
fourth quarter to
assist in the production from wells that are currently producing in the area.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We expect the 
industry will be very active in this area in the upcoming winter, making access 
to
drilling and completion rigs very competitive. We believe Paramount is well 
positioned to operate
in this competitive environment with our long-term rig arrangements and solid 
drilling prospects.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>GRANDE 
PRAIRIE</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Production volumes 
for the third quarter of 2005 averaged 18 MMcf/d of natural gas and 392 Bbl/d of
oil and natural gas liquids for a total of 3,363 Boe/d. Second quarter 2005 
production volumes
averaged 2,999 Boe/d. Production was up 12&nbsp;percent primarily because there 
were turnarounds at two
plants during the second quarter. Production volumes also increased from new 
well tie-ins with
initial rates of 1.0 MMcf/d.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Third quarter 2004 
production averaged 3,404 Boe/d after adjusting for the Marten Creek property
which was included in the Trust spinout.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The major 
accomplishments for the second quarter were the drilling of 9 (6.3 net) wells 
and the
completing of 6 (4.5 net) wells in spite of adverse field conditions. Third 
quarter capital
spending of $12.7&nbsp;million consisted of $1.3&nbsp;million for land, 
$0.7&nbsp;million for geological and
geophysical, $8.8&nbsp;million for drilling and completions, and 
$1.9&nbsp;million for facilities.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount expects to 
drill up to 7 (5.3 net) more wells before year-end following up on some recent
successes and developing some new opportunities. We forecast to add 5 MMcf/d of 
production by the
end of the year with tie-ins.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>NORTHWEST ALBERTA
/ CAMERON HILLS, NORTHWEST TERRITORIES</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Production, on a 
Boe/d basis, decreased slightly in the third quarter when compared to the second
quarter of 2005. Gas production decreased from 27.2 MMcf/d to 26.9 MMcf/d and 
oil and natural gas
liquids production decreased from 810 Bbl/d to 756 Bbl/d. The decrease in 
production is the result
of natural declines.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Capital expenditures 
for the third quarter of 2005 were $2.8&nbsp;million which included expenditures
for land and geological and geophysical amounting to $2.2&nbsp;million. The 
remaining capital was spent
on drilling and facilities activities started in the first quarter.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Capital expenditures 
for the remainder of the year will be confined to land and trade seismic
purchases in preparation for executing our winter program in the first quarter 
of 2006.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>NORTHWEST 
TERRITORIES / NORTHEAST BRITISH COLUMBIA</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Natural gas 
production from this operating area averaged 25 MMcf/d or 4,125 Boe/d for the 
third
quarter down 12&nbsp;percent from second quarter production of 4,664 Boe/d. The 
decrease is a result of
field declines and well shut-ins for plant maintenance and modifications.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The capital 
expenditure program during the third quarter included the drilling of a new 
location at
K-29A at West Liard. The well, which was spud in August, reached a final total 
measured depth of
3,620 meters and will be completed in the Nahanni formation. Other activity 
included workovers and
recompletions at both West Liard and Liard/Maxhamish. Total capital spent in the
third quarter was
$7.9&nbsp;million compared to $16.5&nbsp;million in the second quarter.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Planned fourth 
quarter capital activities will include the completion and tie-in of the K-29A 
well
at West Liard. Two new locations will be drilled at Clarke Lake targeting Slave 
Point gas.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>SOUTHERN</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Southern 
operations produced 13 MMcf/d of natural gas and 1,421 Bbl/d of oil and natural 
gas
liquids in this quarter for a total of 3,592 Boe/d as compared to 3,517 Boe/d in
the second
quarter.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Capital spending in 
the third quarter was $17.0&nbsp;million, comprised of $3.6&nbsp;million on 
land, $9.4
million on drilling and completions and the remainder on facilities.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount drilled 24 
(14.2 net) wells in Chain, added a new 1,800 horsepower compressor at our
Delia compressor station and built the new spine pipeline for Coalbed Methane 
(&#147;CBM&#148;) production.
The combination of new compression with large diameter pipe will result in a 
flowing pressure of 8
pounds per square inch in our CBM development. Construction was completed on a 
new 1,400
horsepower booster compressor at our Chain gas plant. Lower suction pressure has
already helped to
increase production, and coupled with the commencement of tie-in operations we 
have reached a
milestone of having doubled
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">production in this 
field since taking over operations in 2002. Work will continue through the
fourth quarter to drill, complete and tie-in the remainder of our CBM program.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the United States,
we drilled 3 (1.0 net) wells on the Birdbear trend in North Dakota. Two
higher interest wells came on production, boosting Paramount&#146;s United 
States production to over
1000 Boe/d by the start of the fourth quarter. Paramount continues to expand its
presence in
Montana and North Dakota through our wholly-owned subsidiary Summit Resources 
Inc.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>NORTHEAST ALBERTA
/ HEAVY OIL</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Third quarter 
production averaged 279 Boe/d, comprised of 1.6 MMcf/d of gas and 5 Bbl/d of 
natural
gas liquids, compared with 327 Boe/d in the second quarter. The decline in 
production was the
result of two gas wells that were shut-in waiting for required regulatory 
approvals. The gas wells
resumed production in October.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the
Surmont area, the start up of gas production at the Gas Re-Injection and 
Production
Experiment has been delayed until the fourth quarter because of mechanical and 
control issues. The
compression process of the pilot has been operating intermittently through the 
third quarter and
production will start up as soon as issues are resolved. The decision for 
commercial implementation
remains unchanged at late 2006.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>FINANCIAL</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">After adjusting for 
the Trust Spinout, petroleum and natural gas sales before financial instruments
totaled $99.2&nbsp;million for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, 
as compared to $71.6&nbsp;million
for the comparable period in 2004. The increase is mainly the result of higher 
commodity prices
combined with higher production volumes resulting from a successful drilling 
program. Funds flow
for the third quarter of 2005 totaled $50.5&nbsp;million or $0.77 per basic 
share as compared to $28.7
million or $0.49 per basic share for the third quarter of 2004 after adjusting 
for the Trust
Spinout. The 76&nbsp;percent increase in funds flow is primarily due to higher 
petroleum and natural gas
revenue resulting from higher commodity prices and increased production volumes,
partially offset
by higher operating costs, interest and general and administrative expenses.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount recorded a 
net loss for the current quarter of $69.1&nbsp;million or a loss of $1.05 per 
basic
share as compared to net earnings of $28.8&nbsp;million or $0.49 per basic share
for the third quarter
of 2004 after adjusting for the Trust Spinout. The decrease in earnings is 
mainly the result of
increases in non-cash general and administrative expense related to stock-based 
compensation,
unrealized financial instruments losses and depletion and depreciation partially
offset by an
increase petroleum and natural gas revenue.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
lenders are currently finalizing a scheduled semi-annual review of its borrowing
base. They have indicated that the Company&#146;s credit facility will be 
increased to $189&nbsp;million,
with an effective date of October&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>EQUITY 
ISSUANCE</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;14, 
2005, Paramount completed its private placement of 1,900,000 &#147;flow-
through&#148; common
shares at a price of $21.25 per share for gross proceeds of approximately 
$40.4&nbsp;million sold
through a syndicate of underwriters. The net proceeds from the issuance are 
being used to fund the
Company&#146;s ongoing exploration activities. The equity injection facilitates 
the acceleration of the
West Kaybob development.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>OUTLOOK</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount continues 
to project that a total of $350&nbsp;million will be reinvested in 2005, 
including
the expenditures incurred in the first quarter on the Trilogy assets. 
Paramount&#146;s capital program
is designed to grow production from the initial 20,000 Boe/d at the time of the 
Trust Spinout to
25,000 Boe/d by the end of the year although this timing is now anticipated to 
have been delayed by
at least a month. Paramount continues to forecast cash flow to be approximately 
$270&nbsp;million
($4.09/share). Wet field conditions have
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">delayed the timing of
production additions and as a result, Paramount has approximately 4,000 Boe/d
of deliverability behind pipe and awaiting tie-in which is expected to be 
completed by the end of
the year. We look forward to delivering further value to Paramount shareholders 
by continuing to
provide growth through short and medium term drilling opportunities in each of 
the core producing
areas as well as the longer term projects the Company continues to work on such 
as Colville Lake in
the Northwest Territories and bitumen development projects in northeast Alberta.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 12pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>MANAGEMENT&#146;S
DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS (&#147;MD&#038;A&#148;)</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>The following 
discussion of financial position and results of operations should be read in
conjunction with the Company&#146;s interim unaudited consolidated financial 
statements and related
notes for the three and nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, as well as 
the Company&#146;s audited
consolidated financial statements and related notes and MD&#038;A for the year 
ended December&nbsp;31, 2004.
The date of this MD&#038;A is November&nbsp;2, 2005.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>This MD&#038;A 
contains forward-looking statements within the meaning of applicable securities 
laws.
Forward-looking statements include estimates, plans, expectations, opinions, 
forecasts,
projections, guidance or other statements that are not statements of fact. The 
forward-looking
statements in this MD&#038;A include statements with respect to, among other 
things: Paramount&#146;s
business strategy, Paramount&#146;s intent to control marketing and 
transportation activities, reserve
estimates, production estimates, hedging policies, asset retirement costs, the 
size of available
income tax pools, the Company&#146;s credit facility, the funding sources for 
the Company&#146;s capital
expenditure program, cash flow estimates, environmental risks faced by the 
Company and compliance
with environmental regulations, commodity prices, and the impact of the adoption
of various
Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants Handbook Sections and Accounting 
Guidelines.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Although Paramount
believes that the expectations reflected in such forward-looking statements are
reasonable, undue reliance should not be placed on them because the Company can 
give no assurance
that such expectations will prove to be correct. There are many factors that 
could cause
forward-looking statements to be incorrect, including known and unknown risks 
and uncertainties
inherent in the Company&#146;s business. These risks include, but are not 
limited to: crude oil and
natural gas price volatility, exchange rate and interest rate fluctuations, 
availability of
services and supplies, market competition, uncertainties in the estimates of 
reserves, the timing
of development expenditures, production levels and the timing of achieving such 
levels, the
Company&#146;s ability to replace and expand oil and gas reserves, the sources 
and adequacy of funding
for capital investments, future growth prospects and current and expected 
financial requirements of
the Company, the cost of future asset retirement obligations, the Company&#146;s
ability to enter into
or renew leases, the Company&#146;s ability to secure adequate product 
transportation, changes in
environmental and other regulations, the Company&#146;s ability to extend its 
debt on an ongoing basis,
and general economic conditions. The Company&#146;s forward-looking statements 
are expressly qualified
in their entirety by this cautionary statement. We undertake no obligation to 
update our
forward-looking statements except as required by law.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Included in this 
MD&#038;A are references to financial measures such as funds flow from 
operations
(&#147;funds flow&#148;) and funds flow per Boe. While widely used in the oil 
and gas industry, these
financial measures have no standardized meaning and are not defined by Canadian 
generally accepted
accounting principles (&#147;GAAP&#148;). Consequently, these are referred to as
non-GAAP financial
measures. Funds flow appears as a separate caption on the Company&#146;s 
consolidated statement of cash
flows and is reconciled to net earnings. Paramount considers funds flow a key 
measure as it
demonstrates the Company&#146;s ability to generate the cash necessary to fund 
future growth through
capital investment and to repay debt. However, funds flow should not be 
considered an alternative
to, or more meaningful than, net earnings as determined in accordance with GAAP 
as an indicator of
the Company&#146;s performance.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>In this MD&#038;A,
natural gas volumes have been converted to barrels of oil equivalent (Boe) on 
the
basis of six thousand cubic feet (Mcf) to one barrel (Bbl). Boe may be 
misleading, particularly if
used in isolation. A Boe conversion ratio of 6 Mcf=1 Bbl is based on an energy 
equivalency
conversion method, primarily applicable at the burner tip and does not represent
equivalency at the
wellhead.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Additional 
information on the Company can be found on the SEDAR website at 
</I>www.sedar.com<I>.</I>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount is an 
exploration, development and production company with established operations 
and/or
interests in Alberta, British Columbia, Saskatchewan, the Northwest Territories,
offshore the East
Coast of Canada and in Montana, North Dakota and California in the United 
States. Management&#146;s
strategy is to maintain a balanced portfolio of opportunities, to grow reserves 
and production in
the Company&#146;s core areas while maintaining a large inventory of undeveloped
acreage, to focus on
natural gas as a commodity, and to selectively enter into joint venture 
agreements for high
risk/high return prospects.<BR>
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Significant
Events</B></DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>
EQUITY ISSUANCE</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;14, 
2005, Paramount completed the private placement of 1,900,000 Common Shares 
issued on a
&#147;flow-through&#148; basis at $21.25 per share. The gross proceeds of the 
issue were approximately
$40.4&nbsp;million.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>TRUST SPINOUT</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At a special meeting 
held on March&nbsp;28, 2005, Paramount&#146;s shareholders and optionholders 
approved
the trust spinout arrangement under the Business Corporations Act (Alberta) as 
set out in
Paramount&#146;s Information Circular dated February&nbsp;28, 2005 (the 
&#147;Trust Spinout&#148;). Through the plan
of arrangement, shareholders of Paramount received in exchange for their Common 
Shares, one New
Common Share of Paramount and one trust unit (&#147;Trust Unit&#148;) of the new
energy trust, Trilogy Energy
Trust (&#147;Trilogy&#148; or the &#147;Trust&#148;). Upon completion of the 
transaction, shareholders of Paramount
owned all the issued and outstanding New Common Shares and 81&nbsp;percent of 
the issued and outstanding
Trust Units, with the remaining 19&nbsp;percent of the issued and outstanding 
Trust Units being held by
Paramount.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On March&nbsp;29, 
2005 Paramount received the final order of the Court of Queen&#146;s Bench 
approving the
above arrangement (&#147;Plan of Arrangement&#148;), which became effective 
April&nbsp;1, 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At the effective date
of the Plan of Arrangement, the Trust Spinout did not result in a substantive
change in ownership of the property transferred to Trilogy (the &#147;Spinout 
Assets&#148;) under GAAP and
therefore, the transaction was accounted for at the carrying value of the net 
assets transferred
and did not give rise to a gain or loss in the consolidated financial statements
of Paramount.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Spinout Assets 
are located in the Kaybob and Marten Creek areas of Alberta. As holders of
Trust Units after the Plan of Arrangement, the unitholders receive monthly 
distributions of the
cash flow generated by the Spinout Assets held by Trilogy Energy LP, a limited 
partnership, and
distributed to unitholders through the Trust.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Trust Spinout was
completed on April&nbsp;1, 2005 and, as a result, the Company&#146;s 
consolidated
statements of earnings (loss)&nbsp;and retained earnings and statements of cash 
flows for the nine
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 and for the three and nine months ended 
September&nbsp;30, 2004 include
results of operations and cash flows of the Spinout Assets.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The following table 
has been prepared to provide readers an understanding of the impact of the
Trust Spinout on the key operating results when comparing such results for the 
three and nine
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 to the same period in the prior year. 
Paramount considers the pro
forma key operating results presented below to be meaningful, as a significant 
portion of
Paramount&#146;s properties and the production therefrom were transferred to 
Trilogy on April&nbsp;1, 2005
under the Trust Spinout. Amounts under the captions &#147;Spinout Assets&#148; 
and &#147;Pro forma&#148; may not be
indicative of actual results had the Trust Spinout occurred at a date earlier 
than April&nbsp;1, 2005.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>NOTES 
EXCHANGE</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As a condition to the
Trust Spinout described above, on February&nbsp;7, 2005, Paramount completed a
note exchange offer and consent solicitation, issuing approximately 
US$213.6&nbsp;million (Cdn$248.3
million), 8 1/2&nbsp;percent Senior Notes due 2013 (the &#147;2013 Notes&#148;) 
and paying aggregate cash
consideration of approximately US$36.2&nbsp;million (Cdn$45.1&nbsp;million) in 
exchange for approximately
99.31&nbsp;percent of the outstanding <BR>
7 7/8&nbsp;percent Senior Notes due 2010 (the &#147;2010 Notes&#148;) and 100
percent of the outstanding 8 7/8&nbsp;percent Senior Notes due 2014 (the 
&#147;2014 Notes&#148;) and the note
holders&#146; consent to proceed with the Trust Spinout. The premiums paid with 
respect to the notes
exchange and consent solicitation, together with the related deferred financing 
charges, were
charged to income. As at September&nbsp;30, 2005, all of the 2010 Notes and 2014
Notes have been repaid
as a result of the note exchange and subsequent open market purchases. Details 
of the outstanding
notes are discussed further in the Liquidity and Capital Resources section of 
this MD&#038;A.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>INTEREST IN OIL 
SANDS PARTNERSHIP</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the first 
quarter of 2005, Paramount and North American Oil Sands Corporation 
(&#147;NAOSC&#148;)
formed a 50-50 owned partnership (the &#147;Oil Sands Partnership&#148;), for 
the purpose of acquiring,
drilling and evaluating oil sands interests in the central portion of the 
Athabasca Oil Sands
region of Alberta. The formation of the Oil Sands Partnership was completed 
through a series of
related events, the net impact to Paramount of which is primarily the 
contribution of lands in the
Athabasca region of Alberta with a total net book value of approximately 
$9.6&nbsp;million to the Oil
Sands Partnership in exchange for the issuance of partnership units by the Oil 
Sands Partnership to
Paramount.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount initially 
retained a one percent gross overriding royalty interest in some of the lands
contributed to the Oil Sands Partnership in accordance with the partnership 
agreement. On March
21, 2005, Paramount contributed this royalty interest to the Oil Sands 
Partnership in exchange for
additional partnership units after NAOSC acquired additional partnership units 
for cash as required
by the partnership agreement.
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Subsequent to the 
formation of the Oil Sands Partnership, Paramount also entered into purchase and
sale agreements with NAOSC whereby the Company acquired a 50&nbsp;percent 
interest in certain lands for
$10.4&nbsp;million and disposed of a 50&nbsp;percent interest in other lands for
$1.1&nbsp;million. It is
intended that these jointly owned lands will be contributed to the Oil Sands 
Partnership in
exchange for partnership units.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>INTEREST IN GAS 
MARKETING LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In March&nbsp;2005, 
Paramount completed a transaction whereby it acquired an indirect 
25&nbsp;percent
interest in a gas marketing limited partnership for US$5.0&nbsp;million 
(Cdn$6.2&nbsp;million). The gas
marketing limited partnership commenced operations on March&nbsp;9, 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In conjunction with 
the acquisition of this equity interest, Paramount will make available for
delivery an average of 150,000 GJ/d of natural gas over a five-year term, to be 
marketed on
Paramount&#146;s behalf by the gas marketing limited partnership.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount and Trilogy
Energy LP have entered into a Call on Production Agreement whereby Paramount
will have the right to purchase all or any portion of Trilogy Energy LP&#146;s 
available gas production
at a price no less favorable than the price Paramount will receive on the resale
of the natural gas
to the gas marketing limited partnership. The term of the Call on Production 
Agreement is no
longer than five years.
</DIV>

<TR style="font-size: 1px">
    <TD colspan="13" align="left" style="border-top: 3px double 
#000000">&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>
<!-- End Table Body -->
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1)</SUP>See
Significant Events &#151; Trust Spinout for basis of presentation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(2)</SUP> Before financial instruments.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Natural gas revenue 
before financial instruments for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005
decreased 36&nbsp;percent to $80.0&nbsp;million from $125.3&nbsp;million for the
same period in 2004. The
decrease in natural gas revenue resulted primarily from a decrease in production
levels offset
partially by higher natural gas prices. Natural gas production volumes for the 
three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 decreased 50&nbsp;percent to average 99 MMcf/d as 
compared to 196 MMcf/d for the
comparable quarter in 2004. The decrease in production, which was due to the 
Trust Spinout,
resulted in a $78.6&nbsp;million decrease in natural gas revenue for the third 
quarter of 2005 as
compared to the same quarter in 2004. The average natural gas price of $8.80/Mcf
for the three
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 was 27&nbsp;percent higher than the average
natural gas price of
$6.95/Mcf for the same period in 2004. Higher natural gas prices before 
financial instruments
resulted in a $33.3&nbsp;million increase to natural gas revenue for the third 
quarter of 2005 as
compared to the same quarter in 2004. Gas production for the three months ended 
September&nbsp;30, 2005
averaged 99 MMcf/d as compared to 92 MMcf/d on a pro forma basis in 2004. This 
increase in
production was the result of new production from the Company&#146;s drilling 
program. Natural gas price
before financial instruments averaged $8.80/Mcf during the third quarter of 2005
as compared to
$6.83/Mcf on a pro forma basis during the same quarter in 2004.
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Oil and natural gas 
liquids (&#147;NGL&#148;) revenue before financial instruments for the three 
months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 decreased 52&nbsp;percent to $19.2&nbsp;million from 
$39.6&nbsp;million for the same period in
2004. The decrease in oil and NGL revenue resulted primarily from a decrease in 
production levels
partially offset by higher oil and NGL prices. Oil and NGL production volumes 
for the three months
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 decreased 63&nbsp;percent to average 3,158 Bbl/d 
as compared to 8,446 Bbl/d for
the comparable quarter in 2004. The decrease in production, which was due 
primarily to the Trust
Spinout, resulted in a $32.0&nbsp;million decrease in oil and NGL revenue for 
the third quarter of 2005
as compared to the same quarter in 2004. The average oil and NGL price before 
financial
instruments of $65.95/Bbl for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 was
29&nbsp;percent higher than
the average price of $50.97/Bbl for the same period in 2004. Higher oil and NGL 
prices resulted
in an $11.6&nbsp;million increase to oil and NGL revenue for the third quarter 
of 2005 as compared to
the same quarter in 2004. Oil and NGL production for the three months ended 
September&nbsp;30, 2005
averaged 3,158 Bbl/d as compared to 3,251 Bbl/d on a pro forma basis in 2004. 
The decrease in
production was due primarily to the disposition of properties in southeast 
Saskatchewan during the
third quarter of 2004. Oil and NGL price before financial instruments averaged 
$65.95/Bbl during
the third quarter of 2005 as compared to $46.71/Bbl on a pro forma basis during 
the same quarter in
2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Petroleum and natural
gas sales increased 39&nbsp;percent to $99.2&nbsp;million during the third 
quarter of
2005 from $71.6&nbsp;million on a pro forma basis in the third quarter of 2004 
due mainly to the
increase in natural gas production volume and the increase in petroleum and 
natural gas prices,
partially offset by the decrease in oil and NGL production volume as discussed 
above.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1)</SUP>See Significant Events &#151; 
Trust Spinout for basis of presentation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(2)</SUP>Before financial instruments.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Natural gas revenue 
before financial instruments for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005
decreased 12&nbsp;percent to $289.3&nbsp;million from $328.1&nbsp;million for 
the same period in 2004. The
decrease in natural gas revenue resulted primarily from a decrease in production
levels partially
offset by higher natural gas prices. Natural gas production volumes for the nine
months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 decreased 19&nbsp;percent to average 133 MMcf/d as 
compared to 165 MMcf/d for the
comparable period in 2004. The decrease in production, which was due to the 
Trust Spinout and was
partially offset by the increases in production from 2004 acquisitions and the 
Company&#146;s drilling
program, resulted in a $71.3&nbsp;million decrease in natural gas revenue for 
the first nine months of
2005 as compared to the same period in 2004. The average natural gas price 
before financial
instruments of $7.99/Mcf for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 was 
10&nbsp;percent higher
compared to the average natural gas price of $7.27/Mcf for the same period in 
2004. Higher natural
gas prices resulted in a $32.5&nbsp;million increase in natural gas revenue for 
the first nine months of
2005 as compared to the same period in 2004. On a pro forma basis, gas 
production for the nine
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 averaged 93 MMcf/d as compared to 73 MMcf/d
for the comparable
period in 2004. The increase in production is primarily due to the acquisition 
of certain assets
on June&nbsp;30, 2004 and new production from the Company&#146;s drilling 
program. Natural gas price before
financial
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">instruments on a pro 
forma basis averaged $8.21/Mcf during the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 as compared to $7.13/Mcf during the same period in 2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Oil and NGL revenue 
before financial instruments for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005
decreased 10&nbsp;percent to $78.3&nbsp;million as compared to 
$87.4&nbsp;million for the same period in 2004.
The decrease in oil and NGL revenue resulted primarily from a decrease in 
production levels
partially offset by higher oil and NGL prices. Oil and NGL production for the 
nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 averaged 4,812 Bbl/d as compared to 6,758 Bbl/d for the 
comparable period in
2004. The decrease in production, which was due to the Trust Spinout and the 
disposition of the
Company&#146;s properties in southeast Saskatchewan, resulted in a 
$31.9&nbsp;million decrease in oil and NGL
revenue for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 as compared to the 
same period in 2004. The
oil and NGL price before financial instruments of $59.59/Bbl for the nine months
ended September
30, 2005 was 26&nbsp;percent higher compared to the average price of $47.22/Bbl 
for the same period in
2004. Higher oil and NGL prices resulted in a $22.8&nbsp;million increase in oil
and NGL revenue for
the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005. On a pro forma basis, oil and NGL
production for the
nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 averaged 3,180 Bbl/d as compared to 
3,489 Bbl/d for the
comparable period in 2004. The decrease in production is primarily due to the 
disposition of our
properties in southeast Saskatchewan during the third quarter of 2004. Oil and 
NGL price before
financial instruments on a pro forma basis averaged $62.07/Bbl during the nine 
months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 as compared to $44.75/Bbl during the same period in 
2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Pro forma petroleum 
and natural gas sales increased 40&nbsp;percent to $261.6&nbsp;million during
the nine
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 from $186.2&nbsp;million in the same period
of 2004 due mainly to the
increase in natural gas production volume as discussed above and increases in 
petroleum and natural
gas prices, partially offset by the decrease in oil and NGL production volumes 
as discussed above.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1) </SUP>See Significant Events &#151; 
Trust Spinout for basis of presentation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(2)</SUP>Royalties (net of Alberta Royalty 
Tax Credit) divided by petroleum and natural gas sales.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the three and 
nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, royalties totaled $21.1&nbsp;million 
and
$65.6&nbsp;million, respectively as compared to $30.5&nbsp;million and 
$74.7&nbsp;million, respectively, during
the same periods a year earlier. The decrease in royalties is primarily due to 
the decline in
petroleum and natural gas revenue as discussed above. The royalty rate for the 
three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 was higher at 21&nbsp;percent as compared to 
18&nbsp;percent for the same period in 2004
due mainly to increased royalties on properties in the Northwest Territories. 
Historically, these
properties had lower royalty rates, as the properties were subject to a minimum 
royalty which was
being offset against the capital expenditure credit pool.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Royalties for the 
three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 and pro forma royalties for the nine 
months
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 increased compared to pro forma royalties for the 
comparable periods in
2004 due mainly to the increase in revenue as discussed above. The royalty rate 
for the three
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 was higher at 21&nbsp;percent compared to 
the pro forma royalty rate of
19&nbsp;percent for the same quarter in 2004 due to the reason described in the 
preceding paragraph.
Pro forma royalty rates were stable at 15&nbsp;percent to 16&nbsp;percent for 
the nine months ended September
30, 2005 and 2004. Pro forma royalties as a percentage of revenue were lower 
than as actually
reported because the Spinout Assets had higher royalty rates.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1)</SUP>See Significant Events &#151; 
Trust Spinout for basis of presentation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the three and 
nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, operating costs totaled 
$13.1&nbsp;million
and $54.8&nbsp;million, respectively, compared to $27.1&nbsp;million and 
$64.9&nbsp;million, respectively, during
the same periods a year earlier. For the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 
2005, average operating
costs on a unit-of-production basis, increased by one percent to average 
$7.27/Boe as compared to
$7.18/Boe for the third quarter of 2004. For the nine months period ended 
September&nbsp;30, 2005,
average operating costs on a unit-of-production basis increased eight percent to
$7.45/Boe from
$6.92/Boe for the same period in 2004. The increase for both the quarter and 
nine-month periods is
due to the disposition of lower operating cost properties as part of the Trust 
Spinout, combined
with a general increase in the cost of goods and services in the energy sector. 
Operating costs
per Boe for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 were lower than the 
pro forma operating costs
per unit for the same period in 2004 due mainly to the increase in production 
volumes to cover
fixed operating costs. This is also the main reason for the decrease in pro 
forma operating costs
per unit during the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the 
same period in 2004.
Operating costs for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 were higher 
than the pro forma
operating costs during the same quarter in 2004 due mainly to the increase in 
production volumes
combined with a general increase in the cost of goods and services in the energy
sector. The
increase in pro forma production volumes is the primary reason why pro forma 
operating costs
increased for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the same
period in 2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The decreases in 
reported total transportation costs for the three and nine months ended 
September
30, 2005 compared to the same periods in 2004 are mainly the result of the Trust
Spinout partially
offset by the general increase in transportation tariffs. The increase in 
transportation costs per
unit during the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the same 
period in 2004 was due
mainly to the increase in transportation tariff. The decrease in transportation 
costs per unit
during the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the same period
in 2004 is due
primarily to the increase in production volumes to cover fixed transportation 
costs during the
first six months of 2005, partially offset by the increase in
transportation tariffs during the
third quarter of 2005. Total transportation costs were higher in the three 
months ended September
30, 2005 compared to the same period in 2004 due primarily to higher production 
volumes and the
increase in transportation tariffs. The increase in transportation tariffs is 
also the primary
reason for the increase in transportation costs per unit during the three months
ended September
30, 2005 compared to the same period in 2004 on a pro forma basis. Pro forma 
transportation costs
increased during the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the 
same period in 2004 due
mainly to the increase in pro forma production volumes combined with the 
increase in transportation
tariffs.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1)</SUP>See Significant Events &#151; 
Trust Spinout for basis of presentation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Depletion and 
depreciation expense during the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 
decreased
to $42.5&nbsp;million from $52.4&nbsp;million for the comparable period in 2004 
due mainly to the Trust
Spinout, offset by higher costs of expired mineral leases during the current 
period as noted below.
Depletion and depreciation expense increased from $136.8&nbsp;million for the 
nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004 to $140.5&nbsp;million for the nine months ended 
September&nbsp;30, 2005, primarily due to
a higher depletable base as a result of acquisitions and increased capital 
expenditures, combined
with a higher depletion and depreciation rate, which was partly caused by the 
Spinout Assets which
had a lower rate. Depletion and depreciation expense increased during the three 
months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the same period in 2004 on a pro forma basis
due primarily to the
increase in production volumes and the increase in expired mineral leases as 
described below.
These are also the primary reasons why pro forma depletion and depreciation 
expenses increased for
the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 compared to the same period in 
2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Expired mineral 
leases included in depletion and depreciation expense for the three and nine 
months
periods ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 totaled $9.1&nbsp;million and 
$13.2&nbsp;million, respectively. These
amounts are higher as compared to the expired mineral leases for the three and 
nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004 amounting to $3.1&nbsp;million and $7.8&nbsp;million, 
respectively.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Capital costs 
associated with undeveloped land and exploratory, non-producing petroleum and 
natural
gas properties of $320&nbsp;million are excluded from costs subject to depletion
and depreciation at
September&nbsp;30, 2005 (December&nbsp;31, 2004 &#151; $300&nbsp;million).
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Financial 
Instruments</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount&#146;s 
financial success is contingent upon the growth of reserves and production 
volumes
and the economic environment that creates a demand for natural gas and crude 
oil. Such growth is a
function of the amount of cash flow that can be generated and reinvested into a 
successful capital
expenditure program. To protect cash flow against commodity price volatility, 
the Company will,
from time to time, manage cash flow by utilizing forward commodity price 
contracts. The financial
instrument program is generally for periods of less than one year and would not 
exceed 50&nbsp;percent
of Paramount&#146;s current production volumes.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At September&nbsp;30,
2005, Paramount had the following forward financial contracts in place:

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Unrealized gain 
(loss)&nbsp;on financial instruments pertains to the change in the fair value of
financial instruments as a result of mark-to-market accounting. Realized gain 
(loss)&nbsp;on financial
instruments arises from the actual settlement of financial contracts with 
counterparties. The
significant increase in total gain (loss)&nbsp;on financial instruments is 
primarily the result of
significant increases in market prices of oil and gas relative to the prices 
fixed in forward
financial contracts.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On October&nbsp;25, 
2005, the Company terminated a previously existing physical sales contract to
deliver 10,000 GJ/d of natural gas at an AECO Fixed Price of $9.17/GJ from 
November&nbsp;2005 to March
2006. In conjunction with this transaction, the Company became a party to a 
financial contract
(included above) pertaining to the sale of 10,000 GJ/d of natural gas at an AECO
Fixed Price of
$9.185/GJ from November&nbsp;2005 to March&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company is 
exposed to credit risk from financial instruments to the extent of non-
performance
by third parties, and non-performance by counterparties to swap agreements. The 
Company minimizes
credit risks associated with possible non-performance by financial instrument 
counterparties by
entering into contracts with only highly rated counterparties and controls 
third-party credit risk
with credit approvals, limits on exposures to any one counterparty, and 
monitoring procedures. The
Company sells production to a variety of purchasers under normal industry sale 
and payment terms.
The Company&#146;s accounts receivable are with customers and joint venture 
partners in the petroleum
and natural gas industry and are subject to normal credit risk.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As noted in the 
Significant Events section of this MD&#038;A, Paramount will make available for
delivery an average of 150,000 GJ/d of natural gas over a five-year term, to be 
marketed on
Paramount&#146;s behalf by the 25&nbsp;percent owned gas marketing limited 
partnership. Paramount is not
entitled to demand collateral securities from the gas marketing limited 
partnership to ensure
payment for the gas volumes delivered, but is entitled to other means of 
protection in this regard
including stringent credit and risk management restrictions. The Partners of the
gas marketing
limited partnership have approved a credit and risk policy to manage and 
mitigate major business
risk associated with the
partnership, including reporting requirements to enable the partners to monitor 
the adherence to
the credit and risk policy.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">General and 
administrative expenses before other totaled $5.7&nbsp;million and 
$14.1&nbsp;million for the
three and nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, respectively, as compared 
to $5.9&nbsp;million and $16.0
million recorded for the same respective periods a year earlier. The decrease in
general and
administrative expenses before other expenses is primarily a result of 
normalization of shared
office and administration services between Paramount and the Trust (see Related 
Party Transactions
section below), partially offset by an increase in salaries and benefit costs 
resulting from
increased staffing levels to address the increase in operational activities and 
to ensure
compliance with new corporate and reporting obligations in Canada and the United
States.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On a unit-of-
production basis, general and administrative expenses before other expenses were
$3.15/Boe for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 and $1.92/Boe for 
the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005. For the comparable periods in 2004, general and 
administrative expenses before
other expenses were $1.55/Boe for the three-month period and $1.71/Boe for the 
nine-month period.
The increases on a unit-of-production basis were due mainly to the increase in 
salaries and benefit
costs as mentioned above and lower production levels as a result of the Trust 
Spinout.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Stock-based 
compensation increased significantly to $52.4&nbsp;million and 
$66.2&nbsp;million for the three
and nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, respectively, as compared to 
$1.2&nbsp;million and $2.8
million, respectively, for the same periods in 2004. During the third quarter of
2005, non-cash
stock-based compensation expense of approximately $51.4&nbsp;million was 
recognized in earnings to
reflect the change in the intrinsic value of outstanding stock options as a 
result of the
significant appreciation in the market price of the Company&#146;s common shares
in the quarter.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount is one of 
many participants in a mutual insurance company formed to insure specific
property, pollution liability, control of well and other catastrophic risks of 
its members. The
Company has booked non-cash charges of $1.0&nbsp;million, with respect to a 
premium surcharge that the
Company would have to pay upon a hypothetical withdrawal from its participation 
in the mutual
insurance company and for expected losses. The Company evaluates its risk 
management policies and
procedures on an ongoing basis, including its participation in the mutual 
insurance company.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Interest 
Expense</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Interest expense for 
the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, decreased 12&nbsp;percent to 
$7.2
million from $8.2&nbsp;million for the same period in 2004. The decrease in 
interest expense for the
three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 is due to lower levels of credit 
facility borrowings during
the current quarter compared to the corresponding quarter in 2004. Lower capital
expenditures and
property acquisition costs during the current quarter resulted in lower 
borrowings as compared to
the same period last year.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Interest expense for 
the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 was $20.6&nbsp;million, a 
15&nbsp;percent
increase from $17.9&nbsp;million for the same period in 2004. The increase in 
interest expense for the
nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 is attributable mainly to higher 
average credit facility
borrowing levels during the year-to-date period. The increase in borrowings 
during the first half
of 2005 was a result of the Company&#146;s higher capital expenditure activities
and
borrowings incurred as a result of the US Senior Notes exchange and consent 
solicitation for the
Trust Spinout. The </DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">increase in interest 
expense is also the result of an increase in US Senior
Notes issued to partially finance property acquisitions in 2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Dry Hole 
Costs</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Under the successful 
efforts method of accounting for petroleum and natural gas properties,
costs of drilling exploratory wells are initially capitalized and, if 
subsequently determined to be
unsuccessful, are charged to dry hole expense. Other exploration costs, 
including geological and
geophysical costs and annual lease rentals, are charged to exploration expense 
as incurred. Dry
hole costs for the three and nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 amounted 
to $11.0&nbsp;million and
$16.5&nbsp;million, respectively, as compared to $4.8&nbsp;million and 
$9.0&nbsp;million, respectively, for the
same periods in 2004. Approximately $7.0&nbsp;million of dry hole costs in the 
third quarter of 2005
relate to the write-off of costs related to an exploratory well in British 
Columbia.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Geological and 
geophysical expenses increased during the three and nine months ended 
September&nbsp;30,
2005 to $2.8&nbsp;million and $10.0&nbsp;million, respectively, from 
$0.7&nbsp;million and $6.5&nbsp;million,
respectively, for the same periods in 2004, as result of increased exploratory 
activities for the
Company during the current year.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Income Tax</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Income and other 
taxes recovery amounted to $44.9&nbsp;million for the nine months ended 
September
30, 2005 compared to an expense of $19.7&nbsp;million for the same period in 
2004. The recovery in 2005
resulted primarily from the expense recorded from the first quarter of 2005 
accounting for debt
restructuring charges in conjunction with the deferred deduction of those 
charges for tax purposes,
and losses in the third quarter of 2005 caused primarily by stock-based 
compensation expense,
interest expense and realized loss on financial instruments. The expense in 2004
was due primarily
to higher claims on the Company&#146;s tax pools relative to the accounting 
deductions, mitigated by the
reduction in the statutory rate in 2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Funds Flow and 
Earnings</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the three months
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, funds flow from operations totaled $50.5
million as compared to $74.2&nbsp;million in the comparable period in 2004. The 
32&nbsp;percent decrease in
funds flow is primarily due to lower production volumes as a result of the Trust
Spinout, partially
offset by higher commodity prices and the receipt of distributions from the 
Trilogy Energy Trust
Units held by Paramount.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the nine months 
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, funds flow from operations totaled 
$203.6&nbsp;million as
compared to $203.0&nbsp;million in the comparable period in 2004. The higher 
petroleum and natural gas
sales resulting from higher commodity prices in 2005 partially offset by lower 
production volumes
as a result of the Trust Spinout were primary factors for the consistent amounts
along with other
variances described above.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The net loss for the 
three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 totaled $69.1&nbsp;million compared 
to a net
earnings of $45.8&nbsp;million for the comparable period in 2004. The change 
from net earnings to net
loss is primarily due to lower production as a result of the Trust Spinout, 
increase in stock-based
compensation expense as described above, higher dry hole costs and an unrealized
financial
instrument loss of $40.4&nbsp;million in 2005 compared to a gain of 
$7.9&nbsp;million in 2004, partially
offset by the impact of higher prices of petroleum and natural gas products and 
the future tax
recovery in 2005 as compared to future tax expense in 2004.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The net loss for the 
nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005 totaled $101.7&nbsp;million compared 
to net
earnings of $58.9&nbsp;million for the comparable period in 2004. This change in
net earnings is due
mainly to lower production as a result of the Trust Spinout, the increase in 
stock-based
compensation expense, premiums paid on the notes exchange and consent 
solicitation, the increase in
unrealized financial instrument losses from $3.2&nbsp;million for the nine 
months
ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 to $61.7&nbsp;million for the current period, 
partially offset by the impact of
higher prices of petroleum and natural gas products and a realized foreign 
exchange gain.
</DIV>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net revenues for the 
third quarter of 2005 declined from the second quarter of 2005 mainly due to
the unrealized financial instruments loss of $40.4&nbsp;million that was 
recorded in the third quarter
of 2005 compared to a $17.3&nbsp;million gain in the second quarter, partially 
offset by higher
commodity prices. In addition, royalties were higher at $21.1&nbsp;million 
during the third quarter of
2005 compared to $9.3&nbsp;million in the second quarter of 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Net revenues for the 
second quarter of 2005 declined from the first quarter of 2005 mainly due to
the decrease in production resulting from the Trust Spinout, which was partially
offset by higher
commodity prices and the unrealized gain on financial instruments of 
$17.3&nbsp;million during the
second quarter as compared to an unrealized loss on financial instruments of 
$38.6&nbsp;million during
the first quarter of 2005. In addition, a realized financial instruments loss of
$3.7&nbsp;million was
recorded in the second quarter compared to a realized gain of $10.7&nbsp;million
in the first quarter of
2005. First quarter 2005 net revenues decreased from fourth quarter 2004 net 
revenues mainly due
to financial instrument losses of $27.9&nbsp;million during the first quarter 
compared to the financial
instrument gain of $27.4&nbsp;million in the fourth quarter of 2004. Quarterly 
net revenues between the
fourth quarter of 2003 and the fourth quarter 2004 continued to increase as the 
Company steadily
increased production and commodity prices continued to remain high.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The net loss for the 
third quarter of 2005 was due mainly to the loss on financial instruments,
stock based compensation expense and higher dry hole costs. The net loss for the
first quarter of
2005 was due mainly to the premium on notes exchange and consent solicitation 
costs incurred to
facilitate the Trilogy Trust Spinout. The net loss for the fourth quarter of 
2004 was mainly due
to the recording of stock option liability using the intrinsic value to account 
for stock options
as at December&nbsp;31, 2004.
</DIV>

</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(1) </SUP>&#147;Gross&#148; wells means the
number of wells in which Paramount has a working interest or a royalty interest 
that may be convertible
to a working interest.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 3pt"><SUP style="font-
size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">(2) </SUP>&#147;Net&#148; wells means the 
aggregate number of wells obtained by multiplying each gross well by 
Paramount&#146;s percentage working interest therein.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the nine 
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, Paramount participated in the drilling of 
278
gross wells (149 net) compared to 171 gross wells (130 net) for the comparable 
nine month period in
2004. The total gas wells drilled during the nine months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2005 include 64 gross
(39 net) Coalbed Methane wells drilled during the second and third quarters of 
2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the nine months 
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, exploration and development expenditures totaled
$308.6&nbsp;million, as compared to $207.4&nbsp;million for the same period in 
2004. This increase in
exploration and development expenditures is primarily due to increased 
expenditures in the West
Kaybob area.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Third quarter 
exploration and development expenditures for 2005 totaled $62.3&nbsp;million, as
compared
to $51.1&nbsp;million for the same period in 2004. The increase is primarily due
to the Company&#146;s
Coalbed Methane capital expenditure program in the Horseshoe Canyon Fairway in 
southern Alberta and
an increase in land expenditures in West Kaybob.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Liquidity and 
Capital Resources</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>WORKING 
CAPITAL</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
working capital position as at September&nbsp;30, 2005 was a $31.6&nbsp;million 
deficit
compared to an $8.0&nbsp;million surplus at December&nbsp;31, 2004. This change 
in working capital is
primarily the result of the change in financial instruments from a net asset of 
$19.4&nbsp;million at
December&nbsp;31, 2004 to a net liability of $42.3&nbsp;million at 
September&nbsp;30, 2005. Accounts payable and
the amount due to the Trust decreased by $37.4&nbsp;million from December
2004 to September&nbsp;2005, primarily as a result of the Trust Spinout. In 
addition, accounts payable
decreased because amounts owing on the capital projects were less as a result of
the Spinout and
because the Company is more active during the winter season.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
working capital deficiency will be funded by cash flows from operations and draw
downs from the existing credit facility discussed below. In addition, the 
Company receives
distributions (currently at $0.25 per Trust Unit) each month from the Trilogy 
Energy Trust Units
retained by the Company as a result of the Trust Spinout.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>DEBT</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As at 
September&nbsp;30, 2005, Paramount had approximately US$213.6&nbsp;million 
(Cdn$248.3&nbsp;million)
outstanding principal amount of 8 1/2&nbsp;percent Senior Notes due 2013 (the 
&#147;2013 Notes&#148;). All other
notes have been repaid as at September&nbsp;30, 2005 as a result of the notes 
exchange offer and
subsequent open market purchases. The 2013 Notes are secured by 12,755,845 Trust
Units owned by
Paramount, having a market value of $355.9&nbsp;million as of September&nbsp;30,
2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As at 
September&nbsp;30, 2005, the Company had a $136&nbsp;million committed
revolving/non-revolving term
facility with a syndicate of Canadian banks. Borrowings under the facility bear 
interest at the
lender&#146;s prime rate, bankers&#146; acceptance rate, or LIBOR plus an 
applicable margin dependent on
certain conditions. Advances drawn on the facility are secured by a fixed and 
floating charge over
the assets of the Company, excluding the Trilogy Energy Trust Units. The 
Company&#146;s lenders review
the market value of its Trust Units and amend the credit facility borrowing base
accordingly at the
end of each month. The revolving nature of the facility is due to expire on 
March&nbsp;30, 2006,
subject to extension. If the revolving term of any portion of the credit 
facility is not extended,
that portion of the credit facility will have a term maturity date of one year 
from expiration.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company has 
letters of credit totaling $24.2&nbsp;million outstanding with a Canadian 
chartered bank
as at September&nbsp;30, 2005 (December&nbsp;31, 2004 &#151; 
$28.1&nbsp;million). These letters of credit reduce the
amount available under the Company&#146;s credit facility.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Long-term debt 
decreased to $353.0&nbsp;million at September&nbsp;30, 2005, compared to 
$459.1&nbsp;million at
December&nbsp;31, 2004, primarily as a result of the $190&nbsp;million received 
as part of the Trust Spinout
partially offset by increased borrowings to fund the Company&#146;s 2005 capital
expenditure program.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
lenders are currently finalizing a scheduled semi-annual review of its borrowing
base. They have indicated that the Company&#146;s credit facility will be 
increased to $189&nbsp;million,
with an effective date of October&nbsp;31, 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>SHARE CAPITAL AND
STOCK BASED COMPENSATION</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;14, 
2005, the Company completed the private placement of 1.9&nbsp;million flow-
through common
shares for gross proceeds of approximately $40.4&nbsp;million. The net proceeds 
from this private
placement are being used to fund the Company&#146;s ongoing exploration 
activities.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Pursuant to the Plan 
of Arrangement for the Trust Spinout, all of the Old Paramount Options were
replaced with New Paramount Options and Holdco Options.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">For the three months 
ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, 31,500 New Paramount Options were exercised for a
cash payment from Paramount of $0.7&nbsp;million (2004 &#151; 121,750 options 
for $0.6&nbsp;million). For the
three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, 25,875 Holdco Options were exercised
for a cash payment from
Paramount of $0.4&nbsp;million (2004 &#151; $nil). These amounts were charged to
the corresponding stock
option liability with the difference charged to earnings during the periods.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the three 
months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, 39,875 New Paramount Options were 
exercised for
shares for cash proceeds to Paramount of $0.2&nbsp;million (2004 &#151; $nil). 
The proceeds and
corresponding stock option liability of $0.3&nbsp;million were credited to share
capital.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<P><HR noshade><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As at 
September&nbsp;30, 2005 and November&nbsp;2, 2005, the Company had 66,055,925 
and 66,130,175
outstanding common shares, respectively.
</DIV>

    <TD style="font-size: 6pt">&nbsp;</TD>

    <TD width="3%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>The Company and the Trust also had non-interest bearing cash
advances from/to each other arising from normal business
activities.</TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The net amount due to
the Trust arising from the above related party transactions as at September
30, 2005 was $15.2&nbsp;million, including an accrued payable of 
$7.1&nbsp;million arising from the purchase
of gas in the month of September&nbsp;2005 under the above-mentioned Call on 
Production Agreement, and a
Crown royalty deposit claim of $7.7&nbsp;million which when refunded to 
Paramount will be paid to
Trilogy.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount on behalf 
of the Trust, has issued letters of credit totaling $3.8&nbsp;million as at
September&nbsp;30, 2005. Paramount did not record a receivable as at 
September&nbsp;30, 2005 with respect to
such letters of credit which are set to expire in November&nbsp;2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>GAS MARKETING 
LIMITED PARTNERSHIP</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount sold 
6,601,500 GJs of natural gas to the gas marketing limited partnership for
approximately $51.0&nbsp;million for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 
2005. The transactions have
been recorded at the exchange amounts. A receivable of approximately 
$19.1&nbsp;million from the gas
marketing limited partnership arising from the sale of gas in 
September&nbsp;2005 has been included as
part of accounts receivable as at September&nbsp;30, 2005.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>WILSON DRILLING 
LTD.</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On February&nbsp;1, 
2005, Wilson Drilling Ltd., a 50&nbsp;percent owned subsidiary, sold 721,991 
Trinidad
Energy Services Income Trust units to the Company for $7.9&nbsp;million in 
exchange for a Demand
Promissory Note. This transaction has been recorded at the exchange amount.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Risks and 
Uncertainties</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Companies involved in
the exploration for and production of oil and natural gas face a number
of risks and uncertainties inherent in the industry. The Company&#146;s 
performance is influenced by
many factors, including but not limited to, commodity pricing, transportation 
and marketing
constraints, government regulation and taxation.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Natural gas prices 
are influenced by the North American supply and demand balance as well as
transportation capacity constraints. Seasonal changes in demand, which are 
largely influenced by
weather patterns, also affect the price of natural gas.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Stability in natural 
gas pricing is available through the use of short and long-term contract
arrangements. Paramount utilizes a combination of these types of contracts, as 
well as spot
markets, in its natural gas pricing strategy. As the majority of the 
Company&#146;s natural gas sales
are priced to US markets, the Canada/US exchange rate can strongly affect 
revenue.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Oil prices are 
influenced by global supply and demand conditions as well as by worldwide 
political
events. As the price of oil in Canada is based on a US benchmark price, 
variations in the
Canada/US exchange rate further affect the price received by Paramount for its 
oil.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
access to oil and natural gas sales markets is restricted, at times, by pipeline
capacity. In addition, it is also affected by the proximity of pipelines and 
availability of
processing equipment. Paramount intends to control as much of its marketing and 
transportation
activities as possible in order to minimize any negative impact from these 
external factors.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The oil and gas 
industry is subject to extensive controls, regulatory policies and income taxes
imposed by the various levels of government. These controls and policies, as 
well as income tax
laws and regulations, are amended from time to time. The Company has no control 
over government
intervention or taxation levels in the oil and gas industry; however, it 
operates in a manner
intended to ensure that it is in compliance with all regulations and is able to 
respond to changes
as they occur.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Paramount&#146;s 
operations are subject to the risks normally associated with the oil and gas 
industry
including hazards such as unusual or unexpected geological formations, high 
reservoir pressures and
other conditions involved in drilling and operating wells. The Company attempts 
to minimize these
risks using prudent safety programs and risk management, including insurance 
coverage against
potential losses.
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company 
recognizes that the industry is faced with an increasing awareness with respect 
to the
environmental impact of oil and gas operations. Paramount has reviewed the 
environmental risks to
which it is exposed and has determined that there is no current material impact 
on the Company&#146;s
operations other than as have been reflected and accrued in the financial 
statements; however, the
cost of complying with environmental regulations is increasing. Paramount 
intends to ensure
continued compliance with environmental legislation.
</DIV>
<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

Sensitivity Analysis</B>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The Company&#146;s 
earnings and funds flow are highly sensitive to changes in commodity prices,
exchange rates and other factors that are beyond the control of the Company. 
Current volatility in
commodity prices creates uncertainty as to Paramount&#146;s funds flow and 
capital expenditure budget.
The Company will therefore assess results throughout the year and revise 
estimates as necessary to
reflect most current information. The following post Trilogy Spinout analysis 
assesses the
magnitude of these sensitivities on the Company&#146;s 2005 funds flow using the
following base
assumptions:
</DIV>
